I'm very happy and proud of you. Your house is very nice. I like it a lot. I don't know about you but the first thing I would do is upgrade the security like door striker plate screws from 3/4 inch to 3 inches. The longer screws make it more secure. Also consider replacing the striker plates from the small ones to longer more beefy type that will take a punch. Go around the house and install windows locks and outdoor lighting to illuminate dark areas. Always cut your lawn because an uncut lawn tells criminals you might not be home or are rarely home. Put a lock on your outdoor electrical panel. Criminals like to open your panel box and turn off the power to your house to see if anyone is home, so lock it up. if your front door has glass all over the place replace it with one that is mostly solid wood or covered in steel. It shouldn't be possible to crack a simple window and reach in to unlock the door. Now that you live alone always have a spare key on you when ever you leave your house. believe it or not people lock themselves out of their house a lot. When they do they realize they don't have a spare key anywhere on them. If you plan on hiding a key outside of your house it shouldn't be a simple place. I don't like the idea of hiding a key or having one outside but everyone is different. Best wishes.

In the Armenian culture its encouraged and sometimes even frowned upon for kids to move out before marriage. Before anyone says that's outdated... you can move out for college or in general if you want to its not a law. But I did move back in with my parents after college and then moved out once I got married. this allows you to work and save up because of your limited financial responsibilities (house rent or bills...) and once you are ready to move out you have a big chunk of saving there to help you. I wish everyone could have that opportunity. because it does keep you financially stable and mentally healthy (if your family is your support system) all things we could use.

Congratulations on your house! I bought my house in 2014 and it's amazing to finally live somewhere you own. Please don't forget to buy home owner's insurance. It's not mandatory if you don't have a mortgage but it's so important to have if, god forbid, something tragic happens. A few years after I bought my house we lost some roof shingles in a big storm and my hard wood floors got a serious amount of water dumped on them. My insurance paid for a new roof and helped get my floors back into good condition. Very recently my sister's pipes froze in Texas and a pipe over her master bathroom burst. Thankfully her bathroom is by an outside wall and the burst part of the pipe was facing that wall so the only room damaged was her bathroom. Her insurance is paying to help her get a brand new bathroom. Home ownership comes with unexpected expenses sometimes and if you don't have piles and piles of cash hanging around, home insurance is a good way to help with those expenses.
